            <task-lists disabled sortable>
              <div class="comment-body markdown-body p-0 pt-1 js-comment-body ">
                  <p>On that note, I created vish/stress because memhog was a large image and it does not let us control the rate of consumption of memory.</p>
<p>$ docker run --rm vish/stress --help<br>
Usage of /stress:<br>
-alsologtostderr<br>
log to standard error as well as files<br>
-cpus int<br>
total number of CPUs to utilize<br>
-log_backtrace_at value<br>
when logging hits line file:N, emit a stack trace (default :0)<br>
-log_dir string<br>
If non-empty, write log files in this directory<br>
-logtostderr<br>
log to standard error instead of files<br>
-mem-alloc-size string<br>
amount of memory to be consumed in each allocation (default "4Ki")<br>
-mem-alloc-sleep duration<br>
duration to sleep between allocations (default 1ms)<br>
-mem-total string<br>
total memory to be consumed. Memory will be consumed via multiple allocations.<br>
-stderrthreshold value<br>
logs at or above this threshold go to stderr<br>
-v value<br>
log level for V logs<br>
-vmodule value<br>
comma-separated list of pattern=N settings for file-filtered logging</p>
              </div>
            </task-lists>
          </div>
        </div>

      </div>
    </div>
  </details>


    </div>

        <task-lists disabled sortable>
          <div class="comment-body markdown-body soft-wrap  js-comment-body">
            <p>On that note, I created vish/stress because memhog was a large image and it does not let us control the rate of consumption of memory.</p>
<p>$ docker run --rm vish/stress --help<br>
Usage of /stress:<br>
-alsologtostderr<br>
log to standard error as well as files<br>
-cpus int<br>
total number of CPUs to utilize<br>
-log_backtrace_at value<br>
when logging hits line file:N, emit a stack trace (default :0)<br>
-log_dir string<br>
If non-empty, write log files in this directory<br>
-logtostderr<br>
log to standard error instead of files<br>
-mem-alloc-size string<br>
amount of memory to be consumed in each allocation (default "4Ki")<br>
-mem-alloc-sleep duration<br>
duration to sleep between allocations (default 1ms)<br>
-mem-total string<br>
total memory to be consumed. Memory will be consumed via multiple allocations.<br>
-stderrthreshold value<br>
logs at or above this threshold go to stderr<br>
-v value<br>
log level for V logs<br>
-vmodule value<br>
comma-separated list of pattern=N settings for file-filtered logging</p>
          </div>
        </task-lists>

            <task-lists disabled sortable>
              <div class="comment-body markdown-body p-0 pt-1 js-comment-body ">
                  <p>Rebased and transitioned to <a class="user-mention" data-hovercard-type="user" data-hovercard-url="/users/vishh/hovercard" data-octo-click="hovercard-link-click" data-octo-dimensions="link_type:self" href="https://github.com/vishh">@vishh</a>'s image. But I just saw a burstable fail before a best-effort while running the test. I used to set <code>--eviction-hard</code> to <code>memory.available&lt;500Mi</code> in <code>e2e_service.go</code>, but now it's set via a flag for the test context (see <code>test/e2e/framework/test_context.go.RegisterNodeFlags</code>), and doesn't appear to be set by default. I think not setting it by default probably results in eviction remaining disabled as a feature for e2e_node tests, and as a result pods chew up memory until they get OOM-killed  (which ignores QoS) rather than until they get evicted. I just changed the default to what I used to set in <code>e2e_service.go</code> and am re-testing to see if that helps.</p>
              </div>
            </task-lists>
          </div>
        </div>

      </div>
    </div>
  </details>


    </div>

            <a class="float-left mt-1" data-hovercard-type="user" data-hovercard-url="/users/mtaufen/hovercard" data-octo-click="hovercard-link-click" data-octo-dimensions="link_type:self" href="/mtaufen"><img class="avatar avatar-user" height="28" width="28" alt="@mtaufen" src="https://avatars0.githubusercontent.com/u/903617?s=60&amp;u=edb30b2119f5bde4275d5662d72ce047d1998692&amp;v=4" /></a>

            <h4 class="f5 text-normal d-inline text-gray-dark">
              <strong class="text-gray">
                

  <a class="author link-gray-dark css-truncate-target " show_full_name="false" data-hovercard-type="user" data-hovercard-url="/users/mtaufen/hovercard" data-octo-click="hovercard-link-click" data-octo-dimensions="link_type:self" href="/mtaufen">mtaufen</a>
  

              </strong>
              <span class="text-gray">
                  <a href="#issuecomment-238275862" id="issuecomment-238275862-minimized-permalink" class="link-gray"><relative-time datetime="2016-08-08T15:35:33Z" class="no-wrap">Aug 8, 2016</relative-time></a>
              </span>
            </h4>
            
    <span class="timeline-comment-label tooltipped tooltipped-multiline tooltipped-s" aria-label="This user has previously committed to the kubernetes repository.">
      Contributor
    </span>

            <span
  class="timeline-comment-label tooltipped tooltipped-multiline tooltipped-s"
  aria-label="This user is the author of this pull request.">
  Author
</span>

            <task-lists disabled sortable>
              <div class="comment-body markdown-body p-0 pt-1 js-comment-body ">
                  <p>I've run a few scenarios to start getting a ballpark for the thresholds where I see proper eviction order and where I don't (I'm operating under the assumption that when I don't, it's due to an OOM-kill, but I haven't actually investigated that yet):</p>
<pre><code>Passed:
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;500Mi x1
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;300Mi x1
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;250Mi x1
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;230Mi x1
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;220Mi x1
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;210Mi x1
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;205Mi x1

Failed:
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;203Mi x1
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;201Mi x1
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;200Mi x2
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;100Mi x1
</code></pre>
<p>It seems that failures start to crop up somewhere between a threshold of <code>200Mi</code> and <code>230Mi</code>, currently testing <code>220Mi</code> to see what happens there. <strong>Edit:</strong> Passed at <code>220Mi</code>. I'll keep adding results here as I get them.</p>
              </div>
            </task-lists>
          </div>
        </div>

      </div>
    </div>
  </details>

            <task-lists disabled sortable>
              <div class="comment-body markdown-body p-0 pt-1 js-comment-body ">
                  <p>I'm ok with the thresholds being higher for now. We can lower them in a<br>
subsequent PR.</p>
<p>On Mon, Aug 8, 2016 at 8:36 AM, Michael Taufen <a href="mailto:notifications@github.com">notifications@github.com</a><br>
wrote:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>I've run a few scenarios to start getting a ballpark for the thresholds<br>
where I see proper eviction order and where I don't (I'm operating under<br>
the assumption that when I don't, it's due to an OOM-kill, but I haven't<br>
actually investigated that yet):</p>
<p>Passed:<br>
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;500Mi x1<br>
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;300Mi x1<br>
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;250Mi x1<br>
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;230Mi x1</p>
<p>Failed:<br>
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;200Mi x2<br>
--eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;100Mi x1</p>
<p>It seems that failures start to crop up somewhere between a threshold of<br>
200Mi and 230Mi, currently testing 220Mi to see what happens there.</p>
<p>—<br>
You are receiving this because you were mentioned.<br>

<div class="AvatarStack flex-self-start ">

        <a class="avatar avatar-user" data-skip-pjax="true" data-hovercard-type="user" data-hovercard-url="/users/mtaufen/hovercard" data-octo-click="hovercard-link-click" data-octo-dimensions="link_type:self" href="/mtaufen">
          <img height="20" width="20" alt="@mtaufen" src="https://avatars0.githubusercontent.com/u/903617?s=60&amp;u=edb30b2119f5bde4275d5662d72ce047d1998692&amp;v=4" class=" avatar-user" />
</a>  </div>

    <div class="commit-message pr-1 flex-auto min-width-0">
      <code>
        <a title="Node e2e memory eviction test

This test creates three pods with QoS of besteffort, burstable, and
guaranteed, respectively, which each contain a container that tries to
consume almost all the available memory at a rate of about 12Mi/10sec.

The expectation is that eviction will be initiated when the hard
memory.available&lt;250Mi threshold is triggered, and that eviction will proceed
in the order of besteffort, then burstable. Since guaranteed pods should
only be evicted if something charged to the host uses more resources
than were reserved for it, we currently end the test when besteffort and
burstable have both been evicted.

Note that this commit also sets --eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;250Mi
to enable eviction during tests." data-pjax="true" class="link-gray" href="/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/28693/commits/736f1cb7c3071eeca137c615cc8cc4080a3751c5">Node e2e memory eviction test</a>
      </code>

        <span class="hidden-text-expander inline">
          <button type="button" class="ellipsis-expander js-details-target" aria-expanded="false">&hellip;</button>
        </span>

    </div>

    <div class="text-right pr-1">
      

    </div>

    <div class="pr-1 flex-shrink-0" style="width: 16px;">

        <div class="text-gray no-wrap">Loading status checks&hellip;</div>

    <div class="text-right">
      <code>
        <a href="/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/28693/commits/736f1cb7c3071eeca137c615cc8cc4080a3751c5" class="link-gray">736f1cb</a>

    <div class="Details-content--hidden mt-2">
      <pre class="text-gray ws-pre-wrap">This test creates three pods with QoS of besteffort, burstable, and
guaranteed, respectively, which each contain a container that tries to
consume almost all the available memory at a rate of about 12Mi/10sec.

The expectation is that eviction will be initiated when the hard
memory.available&lt;250Mi threshold is triggered, and that eviction will proceed
in the order of besteffort, then burstable. Since guaranteed pods should
only be evicted if something charged to the host uses more resources
than were reserved for it, we currently end the test when besteffort and
burstable have both been evicted.

Note that this commit also sets --eviction-hard=memory.available&lt;250Mi
to enable eviction during tests.</pre>
    </div>
</div>


        </div>
      </div>
